', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'In addition to reporting financial results in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles in the United States, or GAAP, the\nRegistrant provides pro forma net profit/loss and pro forma net profit/loss per diluted share in the press release as additional information for its operating results. Pro forma net loss has been adjusted to exclude the effects of non-operating\nexpenses and non-cash charges, such as amortization of acquisition-related costs and stock option compensation expense. These measures are not in accordance with, or an alternative for, GAAP and may be different from non-GAAP measures used by other\ncompanies. The Registrant\x92s management believes that this presentation of non-GAAP measures provides useful information to management and investors regarding certain additional financial and business trends relating to its financial condition\nand results of operations. In addition, management uses these measures for reviewing the financial results of the Registrant and for planning and forecasting of future periods. The Registrant has consistently provided these non-GAAP measurements in\nprevious press releases and believes that it is important to provide investors and other interested persons with a consistent basis for comparison between quarters. u'\n', u' ', u'10200 South De Anza Boulevard Cupertino, California 95014 USA', u' ', u'Tel: 408.572.2000', u'\n', u'\xa0\xa0', u'\n', u'www.portal.com', u'\n', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Portal Reports Fiscal\n2005 Second Quarter Results ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Cupertino, CA (September 2, 2004) \x97', u'\nPortal Software, Inc. (Nasdaq: PRSF) today reported financial results for its fiscal 2005 second quarter ended July 30, 2004. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Fiscal 2005 Second Quarter Financial Results ', u' ', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'Revenues for the second quarter of fiscal 2005 were $18.6 million, compared to revenues of $33.2 for the same period last year and $31.2 for the first quarter of fiscal 2005\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'Pro forma net loss for the second quarter of fiscal 2005 was $25.6 million, or $0.60 per diluted share ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'Bookings for the second quarter were $46.3 million compared to bookings of $29.1 for the same period last year and $31.5 for the first quarter of fiscal 2005\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'Deferred revenues at July 30, 2004 were $37.4 million, which increased from $23.8 in the first quarter of fiscal 2005 ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'\xa0', u'\n', u'\x95', u'\n', u'Cash and investments at July 30, 2004 were $83.7 million, down from $89.3 million at the end of the first quarter of fiscal 2005. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'In the second quarter of fiscal 2005, license revenue represented 5 percent of total revenue\nand services revenue represented the remaining 95 percent, versus 34 percent and 66 percent, respectively, in the same period last year. License and services revenues were 16 percent and 84 percent, respectively, in the first quarter of fiscal 2005.\n', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Pro forma net loss for the second quarter of fiscal 2005 was $25.6 million, or\n$0.60 per diluted share. This compares to a pro forma net loss of $2.5 million, or $0.07 per diluted share, in the prior year period and a pro forma net loss of $8.7 million, or $0.21 per diluted share, in the first quarter of fiscal 2005. The pro\nforma net loss in the second quarter of fiscal 2005 excludes stock option compensation benefit of $3.6 million, amortization of acquired intangibles of $0.7 million and an adjustment to restructuring costs of $0.4 million. The pro forma net loss in\nthe second quarter of fiscal 2004 excludes a stock option compensation charge of $23.8 million and amortization of acquired intangibles of $0.7 million. The pro forma net loss in the ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'first quarter of fiscal 2005 excludes a stock option compensation benefit of $3.8 million, amortization of acquired\nintangibles of $0.7 million and restructuring costs of $0.4 million. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Net loss\nfor the second quarter of fiscal 2005 was $22.3 million, or $0.53 per diluted share, in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles (\x93GAAP\x94). This compares with a GAAP net loss of $26.9 million, or $0.74 per diluted share, in\nthe same period last year and a GAAP net loss of $6.0 million, or $0.14 per diluted share, in the first quarter of fiscal 2005. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'\x93Our challenge continues to be achieving predictable and profitable results from our services efforts as we transform to a full solutions provider. We have\nre-doubled our efforts to improve our performance\x94 said John E. Little, Portal\x92s founder and chief executive officer. \x93Although our reported results were lower than we had anticipated, we are encouraged by the level of bookings which\nunderscore our progress in building demand for Portal\x92s end-to-end billing solutions\x94. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Fiscal 2005 Six Month Financial Results & Restatement of First Quarter Results ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Revenue for the six months ended July 30, 2004 were $49.8 million, compared to revenue of $65.3 million for the six months ended August 1, 2003. Pro forma net loss for\nthe first six months of fiscal 2005 was $34.3 million, or $0.81 per diluted share, compared to a pro forma net loss of $4.5 million, or $0.12 per diluted share. Pro forma amounts for the six months of fiscal 2005 exclude $7.3 million stock option\ncompensation benefit, $1.3 million for amortization of acquired intangibles and a $25 thousand restructuring costs benefit. Pro forma amounts for the six months of fiscal 2004 exclude $30.8 million for stock option compensation charges and $1.3\nmillion for amortization of acquired intangibles. The GAAP net loss for the first six months of fiscal 2005 was $28.3 million, or $0.67 per diluted share, compared with a GAAP net loss of $36.7 million, or $1.02 per diluted share, in the same period\nlast year. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'The Company identified out of period adjustments related to the\nfirst quarter of fiscal 2005. The most significant item relates to unaccrued contractor costs in the Company\x92s Japan office in the amount of $724 thousand. As a result, and subject to final Audit Committee review and approval, the Company\nexpects to file an amended Form 10-Q for its first fiscal quarter of 2005 reflecting these adjustments. The Company believes it\x92s GAAP net loss for the first quarter of fiscal 2005 will be adjusted to $6.0 million, or $0.14 per share, compared\nto a net loss of $5.2 million, or $0.12 per share, which was originally reported. On a pro forma basis, excluding stock compensation and amortization of acquired intangibles, the Company believes it\x92s net loss for the first quarter of fiscal\n2005 will be adjusted to $8.7 million, or $0.21 per share, compared to a pro forma net loss of $7.9 million or $0.19 per share, which was originally reported. The above ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'amounts are preliminary and subject to Audit Committee review and approval. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Business Outlook ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'The following statements are based on current expectations and are forward-looking. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Given that\nPortal\x92s transformation to a total solutions company is still underway, and that the nature of the transformation introduces significant volatility to forecasted results. Portal has chosen to temporarily suspend providing guidance. However, the\nCompany believes the following elements will be important indicators of its success: new order flow or bookings and deferred revenue, free cash flow (cash used or provided by operations plus capital expenditures) and service margins. In addition, these adjusted non-GAAP results are among the primary indicators used by management as a basis for planning and forecasting of future periods.\nBecause there are no generally accepted industry standards for presenting non-GAAP results, the methods used by Portal may differ from the methods used by other companies. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'About Portal Software, Inc. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Portal is the leading worldwide provider of billing and revenue management solutions for the global communications and media markets. The\ncompany delivers the only platform for the end-to-end management of customer revenue across offerings, channels, and geographies. Portal\x92s solutions enable companies to dramatically accelerate the launch of innovative, profit-rich services\nwhile significantly reducing the costs associated with legacy billing systems. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Portal is the revenue management partner of choice to the world\x92s leading service providers including: Vodafone, AOL Time Warner, Deutsche Telekom, TELUS, NTT, China Telecom, Reuters, Telstra, China Mobile, Telenor Mobil, and France\nTelecom. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'### ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Forward Looking Statement ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'Statements in this release concerning Portal Software, Inc.\x92s business outlook, future financial and operating results, future expense\nreductions, and Portal\x92s overall future prospects are forward looking statements that involve a number of uncertainties and risks. Factors that could cause actual events or results to differ materially include the following: General business\nand economic conditions and changes in the amount of technology spending by our customers and prospects; the timing or delay in signing, commencement, implementation and performance of projects or contracts or the delivery of products and services\nunder them and revenue recognition issues related to same; market acceptance of Portal\x92s products and services; customer and industry analyst perceptions of Portal and its technology vision and future prospects; fluctuations in the market price\nof Portal stock ', u'\n', u'\n', u'\n', u'that can result in unpredictable compensation expense charges; difficulties in implementing or realizing the benefits of\ncost reduction efforts, such as our ability to sublease or eliminate excess office facilities in a timely and cost effective manner; sales force training and productivity; challenges associated with recruiting, training, and retaining skilled\nmanagement and other personnel; ability to establish, maintain, and effectively implement relationships with system integrators and other strategic resellers and vendors and to manage large multi-party projects involving system integrators and other\nparties; rapid technological changes; competitive factors; and unanticipated delays in scheduled product availability. In addition, the significant Tier 1 transactions Portal has closed and is pursuing are larger, multi-year deals, in which revenue\nmay be recognized over multiple periods which may increase long-term predictability and limit near-term visibility and also involve longer sales cycles. These and other factors are described in detail in our Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal\nyear ended January 31, 2004 and our quarterly reports on Form 10-Q. In addition, the associated costs must be expensed\ncurrently as engineering expense. This conclusion accounted for approximately an additional 1/3 of the total miss. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'License revenues were $890,000 as compared to 5 million in the first quarter. For example, we historically recognize a few million dollars of license revenue each quarter due to subscriber growth. ', u' ', u'\xa0', u' ', u'We are working toward building a business\nthat is expected to generate a larger amount of recurring revenue and a solid base for long-term growth.
